         </section>
      </section>
      <section class="article-section__content" id="aenm202302017-sec-0030">
         
         <h2 class="article-section__title section__title section1" id="aenm202302017-sec-0030-title">3 Conclusion</h2>
         
         <p>In this study, the substitution of Ru in layered Na<sub>x</sub>CoO<sub>2</sub> was investigated. Benefiting from the Ru doping, Na<sub>0.6</sub>[Co<sub>0.78</sub>Ru<sub>0.22</sub>]O<sub>2</sub> delivered a high discharge capacity of 163&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> at 0.1&nbsp;C, which is superior to that of Na<sub>0.67</sub>CoO<sub>2</sub>. Furthermore, using a combination of operando-XRD, X-ray absorption spectroscopy, and theoretical studies, it was demonstrated that the presence of Ru suppresses the formation of Na<sup>+</sup>/ordering in the structure and also activates itself via a Ru<sup>4+</sup>/Ru<sup>5+</sup> and additional O<sup>2−</sup>/(O<sub>2</sub><sup>n−</sup>) redox process in the layered structural framework. As a result, higher capacity is delivered in Na<sub>0.6</sub>[Co<sub>0.78</sub>Ru<sub>0.22</sub>]O<sub>2</sub> owing to the use of both cationic and anionic redox reactions. Our findings indicate the feasibility of designing new high-capacity cathode materials for sodium-ion batteries by using 4<i>d</i> elements.</p>
         </section>
      <section class="article-section__content" id="aenm202302017-sec-0040">
         
         <h2 class="article-section__title section__title section1" id="aenm202302017-sec-0040-title">4 Experimental Section</h2>
         
         <section class="article-section__sub-content" id="aenm202302017-sec-0050">
            
            <section class="article-section__sub-content" id="aenm202302017-sec-0060">
               
               <section class="article-section__sub-content" id="aenm202302017-sec-0070">
                  
                  <h4 class="article-section__sub-title section4" id="aenm202302017-sec-0070-title"> Synthesis</h4>
                  
                  <p>P2-type Na<sub>0.67</sub>CoO<sub>2</sub> (NCO) and Na<sub>0.6</sub>[Co<sub>0.78</sub>Ru<sub>0.22</sub>]O<sub>2</sub> (NCRO) powders were synthesized by the self-combustion method. Stoichiometric amounts of Co(NO<sub>3</sub>)<sub>2</sub>·6H<sub>2</sub>O (98%, Sigma–Aldrich) and NaNO<sub>3</sub> (99.5%, Alfa) were mixed with citric acid (99.5%, Sigma-Aldrich) and sucrose (99.5%, Sigma–Aldrich) in a weight ratio of 1:0.2:0.05 (salts:citric acid:sucrose) in water. The mixture was then stirred for 1&nbsp;h and heated at 120&nbsp;°C to evaporate the solvent. Further dried powders were heated at 220&nbsp;°C to induce self-combustion. The collected powders were preheated at 400&nbsp;°C for 4&nbsp;h in air to remove the residual organics, and the obtained powders were mixed with RuO<sub>2</sub> (ACROS Organics) in an agate mortar. Both the NCO and NCRO powders were calcined at 900&nbsp;°C for 12&nbsp;h in an air gas and then slowly cooled to room temperature.</p>
                  </section>
               
               <section class="article-section__sub-content" id="aenm202302017-sec-0080">
                  
                  <h4 class="article-section__sub-title section4" id="aenm202302017-sec-0080-title"> Characterization</h4>
                  
                  <p>For characterization of the synthesized powders X-ray diffraction was conducted using X'Pert, PANalytical diffractometer with Cu Kα radiation in the scan range from 10° to 80°. Rietveld refinement was performed to analyze the obtained powder XRD patterns using the full proof program.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202302017-bib-0032" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202302017-bib-0032_R_d51655097e2596" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 32 - Phys. B">32</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> The particle morphologies of the synthesized materials were investigated using field-emission scanning electron microscopy (SEM; SU-8010, Hitachi) and high-resolution transmission electron microscopy (TEM; Jeol, JEM-ARM200F) combined with energy-dispersive X-ray spectroscopy (EDX). Operando XRD measurements (<i>o</i>-XRD, X'Pert, PANalytical diffractometer) were conducted to monitor the structural evolution during Na<sup>+</sup> de-/intercalation.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202302017-bib-0033" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202302017-bib-0033_R_d51655097e2605" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 33 - J. Power Sources">33</a>, <a href="#aenm202302017-bib-0034" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202302017-bib-0034_R_d51655097e2605" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 34 - J. Power Sources">34</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> The direct-current electrical conductivity of both NCO and NCRO powders was measured by using the direct volt–ampere method (CMT-SR1000, AIT). Disc samples were contacted with a four-point probe during the measurement process. The atomic ratios of elements in the samples were examined by inductively coupled plasma-atomic emission spectroscopy (ICP-AES; OPTIMA 8300; Perkin-Elmer, USA). X-ray absorption near-edge structure (XANES) spectroscopy measurements were performed at the 8&nbsp;C beamline for the Co K-edge, the 10&nbsp;C beamline for the Ru K-edge, and the 4&nbsp;C beamline for the O K-edge at the Pohang Accelerator Laboratory, South Korea. The Athena software package was used to process the XANES data, as described in the reference.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202302017-bib-0035" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202302017-bib-0035_R_d51655097e2611" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 35 - J. Synchrotron Radiat.">35</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup></p>
                  </section>
               
               <section class="article-section__sub-content" id="aenm202302017-sec-0090">
                  
                  <h4 class="article-section__sub-title section4" id="aenm202302017-sec-0090-title"> Electrochemical Testing</h4>
                  
                  <p>Electrodes were prepared by mixing the active materials (80&nbsp;wt.%), polyvinylidene fluoride (PVDF, 10&nbsp;wt.%), and conducting agent (Super P, 10&nbsp;wt.%) in <i>N</i>-methyl-2-pyrrolidone (NMP) solution. The well-mixed slurry was applied on Al foil using a doctor blade and then dried at 110&nbsp;°C for 24&nbsp;h. Discs were cut out of the dried electrodes (loading mass: ≈3&nbsp;mg&nbsp;cm<sup>−2</sup>). All the procedures for the electrode fabrication and handling were performed in a dry room. Half cells were fabricated in an Ar-filled glovebox, using Na metal as the counter electrode, in an R2032 coin-type cell. The electrolyte solution used was 0.5&nbsp;<span class="smallCaps">m</span> NaPF<sub>6</sub> in a mixture of propylene carbonate (PC) and fluorinated ethylene carbonate (FEC), with a volume ratio of 98:2. The electrochemical performance of each half cell was evaluated by applying a constant current of 23.5&nbsp;mA&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> (0.1&nbsp;C) in the voltage range of 1.5−4.3&nbsp;V at room temperature. Galvanostatic intermittent titration technique (GITT) measurements were performed by applying the repeated current pulses for 30&nbsp;min at a rate of 0.05&nbsp;C (11.75&nbsp;mA&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>) for charge/discharge followed by an open-circuit periods of 1&nbsp;h in the voltage range of 1.5−4.3&nbsp;V. Differential electrochemical mass spectrometry (DEMS) was conducted in a R2032 coin-type. The cell was charged and discharged at a current rate of 23.5&nbsp;mA&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> (0.1&nbsp;C). Ar served as the carrier gas for charge and discharge processes at a flow rate of 15&nbsp;sccm. Gas emissions were measured using HPR-20 R&amp;D <i>O-</i>DEMS (Hiden Analytical).</p>
                  </section>
               
               <section class="article-section__sub-content" id="aenm202302017-sec-0100">
                  
                  <h4 class="article-section__sub-title section4" id="aenm202302017-sec-0100-title"> First-Principles Calculations</h4>
                  
                  <p>Spin-polarized density functional theory (DFT) calculations with the projector augmented wave (PAW)<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202302017-bib-0036" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202302017-bib-0036_R_d51655097e2650" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 36 - Phys. Rev. B">36</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> potential as implemented in the Vienna Ab Initio Simulation Package (VASP)<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202302017-bib-0037" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202302017-bib-0037_R_d51655097e2655" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 37 - Phys. Rev. B">37</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> were performed for the undoped and doped Na<sub>x</sub>CoO<sub>2</sub> materials for both fully charged and discharged states. The geometries of the structures were optimized using the Perdew–Burke–Ernzerhof (PBE)<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202302017-bib-0038" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202302017-bib-0038_R_d51655097e2665" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 38 - Phys. Rev. Lett.">38</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> functional and an electronic convergence criterion of 10<sup>−4</sup>&nbsp;eV as well as a force convergence criterion of 2&nbsp;×&nbsp;10<sup>−2</sup>&nbsp;eV&nbsp;Å<sup>−1</sup>. PAW potentials containing only the valence electrons of the considered elements were used, and the energy cut off was set to 520&nbsp;eV. The electronic structures were determined by single-point calculations with the Heyd–Scuseria–Ernzerhof (HSE) 06<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202302017-bib-0039" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202302017-bib-0039_R_d51655097e2677" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 39 - J. Chem. Phys.">39</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> functional. As the first step, four electronic optimizations with different initial magnetic moments (number of unpaired electrons) considering different redox activities of the metal ions as well as high- or low-spin configurations for cobalt ions were performed for each compound (Table <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S3</a>, Supporting Information). An electronic convergence criterion of 10<sup>−2</sup>&nbsp;eV was used, and the structures with the lowest energies were further converged to 10<sup>−4</sup>&nbsp;eV for the final analysis. The Na and Ru contents as well as the structure types were adjusted to the experimental findings, resulting in the following models: Na<sub>0.75</sub>CoO<sub>2</sub> (P2), Na<sub>0.25</sub>CoO<sub>2</sub> (P2), Na<sub>0.69</sub>Ru<sub>0.25</sub>Co<sub>0.75</sub>O<sub>2</sub> (P2), and Na<sub>0.06</sub>Ru<sub>0.25</sub>Co<sub>0.75</sub>O<sub>2</sub> (OP4). Supercells of 4&nbsp;×&nbsp;2&nbsp;×&nbsp;1 (<i>k</i>-point mesh: 2&nbsp;×&nbsp;4&nbsp;×&nbsp;2) were used for the P2 phases, and a 2&nbsp;×&nbsp;2&nbsp;×&nbsp;1 (<i>k</i>-point mesh: 4&nbsp;×&nbsp;4&nbsp;×&nbsp;1) supercell was used for the OP4 phase, containing 16 formula units each. For the electronic-structure calculations, Na<sub>0.06</sub>Ru<sub>0.25</sub>Co<sub>0.75</sub>O<sub>2</sub> was also modeled in the P2 phase, assuming that the inter-layer interactions could be neglected for the electronic structures. An HSE optimization with 10<sup>−3</sup>&nbsp;eV electronic and 4&nbsp;×&nbsp;10<sup>−2</sup>&nbsp;eV&nbsp;Å<sup>−1</sup> force convergence criteria as well as a reduced <i>k</i>-point grid of 1&nbsp;×&nbsp;2&nbsp;×1 was performed for the P2 structure. The electronic structures of desodiated NCRO were obtained using this P2 model. The arrangements of the Na, Ru, and Co ions were determined using a coulomb-energy analysis with the help of the so-called supercell code.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202302017-bib-0040" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202302017-bib-0040_R_d51655097e2737" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 40 - J. Cheminf.">40</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> The following charges were applied for the analysis: −2 for oxygen, +1 for sodium, +3 for cobalt, and +4 for ruthenium. The required additional positive charges for the charge balance were assigned evenly to cobalt and ruthenium ions. All possible Na arrangements were iterated together with the Ru and Co arrangements, and all possible distributions of Na ions between the two different P sites were considered, resulting in a full screening of all possible configurations, in total ≈10<sup>12</sup> structures including symmetry equivalents. Atomistic structures were visualized with the VESTA software package,<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202302017-bib-0041" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202302017-bib-0041_R_d51655097e2745" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 41 - J. Appl. Crystallogr.">41</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> and spin-density differences were calculated using the Vaspkit software.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202302017-bib-0042" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202302017-bib-0042_R_d51655097e2750" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 42 - Comput. Phys. Commun.">42</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup></p>
                  </section>
               </section>
            </section>
         </section>

title="OpenURL Imperial College London" class="sfxLink visitable" target="_blank">Find at Imperial</a></span></div></li>
                  
                  <li data-bib-id="aenm202302017-bib-0003"><span class="bullet">3</span><span class="author">C. Delmas</span>, <span class="author">J.-J. Braconnier</span>, <span class="author">C.
